We also monitored the &lt;i&gt;r&lt;i/&gt;-band variability of the two quasar images (A and B) with the LT over 143 epochs in the period 2009\u20132016. These new data in both the wavelength and time domains have confirmed that the system is an unusual microlensing factory. The C\u2009iv emission line is remarkably microlensed, since the microlensing magnification of B relative to that for A, &lt;i&gt;\u03bc&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;BA&lt;sub/&gt;, reaches a value of 1.4 (~0.4 mag) for its core. Moreover, the B image shows a red wing enhancement of C\u2009iv flux (relative to A), and &lt;i&gt;\u03bc&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;BA&lt;sub/&gt; = 2 (0.75 mag) for the C\u2009iv broad-line emission. Regarding the nuclear continuum, we find a chromatic behaviour of &lt;i&gt;\u03bc&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;BA&lt;sub/&gt;, which roughly varies from ~5 (1.75 mag) at 7000 \u00c5 to ~6 (1.95 mag) at 4000 \u00c5. We also detect significant microlensing variability in the &lt;i&gt;r&lt;i/&gt; band, and this includes a number of microlensing events on timescales of 50\u2013100 d. Fortunately, the presence of an intrinsic 0.7 mag dip in the light curves of A and B, permitted us to measure the time delay between both quasar images. This delay is \u0394&lt;i&gt;t&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;AB&lt;sub/&gt; = 47&lt;sup&gt;+5&lt;sup/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;-6&lt;sub/&gt; d (1&lt;i&gt;\u03c3&lt;i/&gt; confidence interval; A is leading), in good agreement with predictions of lens models.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_funding_source\" content=\"citation_funder=Spanish Department of Research, Development and Innovation; citation_grant_number=AYA2013-47744-C3-2-P;\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_funding_source\" content=\"citation_funder=Universidad de Cantabria; citation_funder_id=http://dx.doi.org/10.13039/501100006365;\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=C. Shalyapin\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_author_institution\" content=\"Departamento de F\u00edsica Moderna, Universidad de Cantabria, Avda. de Los Castros s/n, 39005 Santander, Spain\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_author_institution\" content=\"Institute for Radiophysics and Electronics, National Academy of Sciences of Ukraine, 12 Proskura St., 61085 Kharkov, Ukraine\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_title\" content=\"Gravitational lens system SDSS J1339+1310: microlensing factory and time delay\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/12/02\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/12/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"596\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_firstpage\" content=\"A77\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_doi\" content=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201628790\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_bibcode\" content=\"2016A%26A...596A..77G\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/abs/2016/12/aa28790-16/aa28790-16.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_fulltext_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/full_html/2016/12/aa28790-16/aa28790-16.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_pdf_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/12/aa28790-16.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: micro\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"quasars: individual: SDSS J1339+1310\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"cosmological parameters\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"We spectroscopically re-observed the gravitational lens system SDSS J1339+1310 using OSIRIS on the GTC. We also monitored the &lt;i&gt;r&lt;i/&gt;-band variability of the two quasar images (A and B) with the LT over 143 epochs in the period 2009\u20132016. These new data in both the wavelength and time domains have confirmed that the system is an unusual microlensing factory. The C\u2009iv emission line is remarkably microlensed, since the microlensing magnification of B relative to that for A, &lt;i&gt;\u03bc&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;BA&lt;sub/&gt;, reaches a value of 1.4 (~0.4 mag) for its core. Moreover, the B image shows a red wing enhancement of C\u2009iv flux (relative to A), and &lt;i&gt;\u03bc&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;BA&lt;sub/&gt; = 2 (0.75 mag) for the C\u2009iv broad-line emission. Regarding the nuclear continuum, we find a chromatic behaviour of &lt;i&gt;\u03bc&lt;i/&gt;&lt;sub&gt;BA&lt;sub/&gt;, which roughly varies from ~5 (1.75 mag) at 7000 \u00c5 to ~6 (1.95 mag) at 4000 \u00c5. We also detect significant microlensing variability in the &lt;i&gt;r&lt;i/&gt; band, and this includes a number of microlensing events on timescales of 50\u2013100 d. Fortunately, the presence of an intrinsic 0.7 mag dip in the light curves of A and B, permitted us to measure the time delay between both quasar images.
